The output is valid JSON and complete. Here is a summary of what was found and written to `/workspace/answer.json`:

---

## Findings

### CSS calc() Parsing — Rust (Servo/Stylo), not C++

Firefox's Stylo integration means **all CSS calc() parsing is done in Rust**. There is no C++ `nsCSSParser` calc() implementation in this codebase.

| File | Role |
|---|---|
| `servo/components/style/values/specified/calc.rs` (1354 lines) | Tokenises and parses raw CSS `calc()` source into a typed AST. Handles the full CSS Values Level 4 math-function grammar: `calc()`, `min()`, `max()`, `clamp()`, `round()`, `mod()`, `rem()`, trig functions, etc. |
| `servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs` (2042 lines) | Defines the generic `CalcNode<L>` AST and implements resolution. Contains all **NaN, infinity, and overflow handling** at the Rust level (lines 390–407, 987–1079, 1249–1258, 1401–1414, 1535–1542). |
| `servo/ports/geckolib/glue.rs` | FFI bridge: exports `Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage` (line 9208) and `Servo_ResolveAnchorFunctionsInCalcPercentage` (line 9229) to C++. |

---

### Numeric Overflow During calc() Resolution — 17 C++ Files

After Servo resolves `calc()` to a `float`, C++ converts it to `nscoord` (`int32_t`, bounded by `nscoord_MAX = (1<<30)−1`). Overflow is handled in layers:

**Layer 1 — Float-to-nscoord conversion primitives (`gfx/src/nsCoord.h`)**
- `NSToCoordRoundWithClamp()` (lines 108–128): bounds-checks `>= nscoord_MAX` / `<= nscoord_MIN` before cast
- `NSToCoordTruncClamped()` (lines 268–288): same, with truncation

**Layer 2 — Servo wrapper (`layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h`)**
- `DefaultLengthToAppUnits()` (lines 545–556): explicit `>= nscoord_MAX` / `<= nscoord_MIN` guards before rounding
